Please provide a value in [0,1] range.\\\"\\n42:         )\\n43: \\n44:     @torch.no_grad()\\n45:     def ema_update(ema_param_list: PARAM_LIST, current_param_list: PARAM_LIST, _):\\n46:         # foreach lerp only handles float and complex\\n47:         if torch.is_floating_point(ema_param_list[0]) or torch.is_complex(\\n48:             ema_param_list[0]\\n49:         ):\\n50:             torch._foreach_lerp_(ema_param_list, current_param_list, 1 - decay)\\n51:         else:\\n52:             for p_ema, p_model in zip(ema_param_list, current_param_list):\\n53:                 p_ema.copy_(p_ema * decay + p_model * (1 - decay))\\n54: \\n55:     return ema_update\\n56: \\n57: \\n58: def get_swa_multi_avg_fn():\\n59:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Get the function applying stochastic weight average (SWA) across multiple params.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n60: \\n61:     @torch.no_grad()\\n62:     def swa_update(\\n63:         averaged_param_list: PARAM_LIST,\\n64:         current_param_list: PARAM_LIST,\\n65:         num_averaged: Union[Tensor, int],\\n66:     ):\\n67:         # foreach lerp only handles float and complex\\n68:         if torch.is_floating_point(averaged_param_list[0]) or torch.is_complex(\\n69:             averaged_param_list[0]\\n70:         ):\\n71:             torch._foreach_lerp_(\\n72:                 averaged_param_list,\\n73:                 current_param_list,\\n74:                 cast(float, 1 / (num_averaged + 1)),\\n75:             )\\n76:         else:\\n77:             diffs = torch._foreach_sub(current_param_list, averaged_param_list)\\n78:             if isinstance(num_averaged, Tensor):\\n79:                 torch._foreach_addcdiv_(\\n80:                     averaged_param_list,\\n81:                     diffs,\\n82:                     [num_averaged + 1] * len(averaged_param_list),\\n83:                 )\\n84:             else:\\n85:                 torch._foreach_add_(\\n86:                     averaged_param_list, diffs, alpha=1.0 / (num_averaged + 1)\\n87:                 )\\n88: \\n89:     return swa_update\\n90: \\n91: \\n92: def get_ema_avg_fn(decay=0.999):\\n93:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Get the function applying exponential moving average (EMA) across a single param.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n94: \\n95:     if decay < 0.0 or decay > 1.0:\\n96:         raise ValueError(\\n97:             f\\\"Invalid decay value {decay} provided. the function must take in the current value of the\\n140:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameter, the current value of :attr:`model`\\n141:             parameter, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\\n142:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\\n143:         multi_avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\\n144:             parameters inplace; the function must take in the current values of the\\n145:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameters as a list, the current values of :attr:`model`\\n146:             parameters as a list, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\\n147:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\\n148:         use_buffers (bool): if ``True``, it will compute running averages for\\n149:             both the parameters and the buffers of the model. (default: ``False``)\\n150: \\n151:     Example:\\n152:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\\\"undefined variables\\\")\\n153:         >>> loader, optimizer, model, loss_fn = ...\\n154:         >>> swa_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model)\\n155:         >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(optimizer,\\n156:         >>>                                     T_max=300)\\n157:         >>> swa_start = 160\\n158:         >>> swa_scheduler = SWALR(optimizer, swa_lr=0.05)\\n159:         >>> for i in range(300):\\n160:         >>>      for input, target in loader:\\n161:         >>>          optimizer.zero_grad()\\n162:         >>>          loss_fn(model(input), target).backward()\\n163:         >>>          optimizer.step()\\n164:         >>>      if i > swa_start:\\n165:         >>>          swa_model.update_parameters(model)\\n166:         >>>          swa_scheduler.step()\\n167:         >>>      else:\\n168:         >>>          scheduler.step()\\n169:         >>>\\n170:         >>> # Update bn statistics for the swa_model at the end\\n171:         >>> torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn(loader, swa_model)\\n172: \\n173:     You can also use custom averaging functions with the `avg_fn` or `multi_avg_fn` parameters.\\n174:     If no averaging function is provided, the default is to compute\\n175:     equally-weighted average of the weights (SWA).\\n176: \\n177:     Example:\\n178:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\\\"undefined variables\\\")\\n179:         >>> # Compute exponential moving averages of the weights and buffers\\n180:         >>> ema_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model,\\n181:         >>>             torch.optim.swa_utils.get_ema_multi_avg_fn(0.9), use_buffers=True)\\n182: \\n183:     .. note::\\n184:         When using SWA/EMA with models containing Batch Normalization you may\\n185:         need to update the activation statistics for Batch Normalization.\\n186:         This can be done either by using the :meth:`torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn`\\n187:         or by setting :attr:`use_buffers` to `True`. The first approach updates the\\n188:         statistics in a post-training step by passing data through the model. The\\n189:         second does it during the parameter update phase by averaging all buffers.\\n190:         Empirical evidence has shown that updating the statistics in normalization\\n191:         layers increases accuracy, but you may wish to empirically test which\\n192:         approach yields the best results in your problem.\\n193: \\n194:     .. note::\\n195:         :attr:`avg_fn` and `multi_avg_fn` are not saved in the :meth:`state_dict` of the model.\\n196: \\n197:     .. note::\\n198:         When :meth:`update_parameters` is called for the first time (i.e.\\n199:         :attr:`n_averaged` is `0`) the parameters of `model` are copied\\n200:         to the parameters of :class:`AveragedModel`. For every subsequent\\n201:         call of :meth:`update_parameters` the function `avg_fn` is used\\n202:         to update the parameters.\\n203: \\n204:     .. _Averaging Weights Leads to Wider Optima and Better Generalization:\\n205:         https://arxiv.org/abs/1803.05407\\n206:     .. _There Are Many Consistent Explanations of Unlabeled Data: Why You Should\\n207:         Average:\\n208:         https://arxiv.org/abs/1806.05594\\n209:     .. _SWALP: Stochastic Weight Averaging in Low-Precision Training:\\n210:         https://arxiv.org/abs/1904.11943\\n211:     .. _Stochastic Weight https://paperswithcode.com/method/polyak-averaging\\n216:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n217: \\n218:     n_averaged: Tensor\\n219: \\n220:     def __init__(\\n221:         self,\\n222:         model: self.module = deepcopy(model)\\n235:         if device is not None:\\n236:             self.module = self.module.to(device)\\n237:         self.register_buffer(\\n238:             \\\"n_averaged\\\", update_parameters(self, model: Module):\\n249:         \\\"\\\"\\\"Update model parameters.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n250:         self_param = (\\n251:             itertools.chain(self.module.parameters(), the function must take in the current value of the\\n140:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameter, the current value of :attr:`model`\\n141:             parameter, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\\n142:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\\n143:         multi_avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\\n144:             parameters inplace; the function must take in the current values of the\\n145:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameters as a list, the current values of :attr:`model`\\n146:             parameters as a list, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\\n147:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\\n148:         use_buffers (bool): if ``True``, it will compute running averages for\\n149:             both the parameters and the buffers of the model. (default: ``False``)\\n150: \\n151:     Example:\\n152:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\\\"undefined variables\\\")\\n153:         >>> loader, optimizer, model, loss_fn = ...\\n154:         >>> swa_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model)\\n155:         >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(optimizer,\\n156:         >>>                                     T_max=300)\\n157:         >>> swa_start = 160\\n158:         >>> swa_scheduler = SWALR(optimizer, swa_lr=0.05)\\n159:         >>> for i in range(300):\\n160:         >>>      for input, target in loader:\\n161:         >>>          optimizer.zero_grad()\\n162:         >>>          loss_fn(model(input), target).backward()\\n163:         >>>          optimizer.step()\\n164:         >>>      if i > swa_start:\\n165:         >>>          swa_model.update_parameters(model)\\n166:         >>>          swa_scheduler.step()\\n167:         >>>      else:\\n168:         >>>          scheduler.step()\\n169:         >>>\\n170:         >>> # Update bn statistics for the swa_model at the end\\n171:         >>> torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn(loader, swa_model)\\n172: \\n173:     You can also use custom averaging functions with the `avg_fn` or `multi_avg_fn` parameters.\\n174:     If no averaging function is provided, the default is to compute\\n175:     equally-weighted average of the weights (SWA).\\n176: \\n177:     Example:\\n178:         >>> # The first approach updates the\\n188:         statistics in a post-training step by passing data through the model. The\\n189:         second does it during the parameter update phase by averaging all buffers.\\n190:         Empirical evidence has shown that updating the statistics in normalization\\n191:         layers increases accuracy, but you may wish to empirically test which\\n192:         approach yields the best results in your problem.\\n193: \\n194:     .. note::\\n195:         :attr:`avg_fn` and `multi_avg_fn` are not saved in the :meth:`state_dict` of the model.\\n196: \\n197:     .. note::\\n198:         When :meth:`update_parameters` is called for the first time (i.e.\\n199:         :attr:`n_averaged` is `0`) the parameters of `model` are copied\\n200:         to the parameters of :class:`AveragedModel`. The :class:`SWALR` scheduler can be used together with other\n392:     schedulers to switch to a constant learning rate late in the training\n393:     as in the example below.\n394: \n395: This is in contrast to some other\\n242:         frameworks that initialize it to all zeros. One notable side effect\\n243:         of this decision is that the first momentum value will not be scaled\\n244:         by dampening. Dampening will be applied starting at the second step.\\n245: \\n246:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n247: )\\n248: \\n249: \\n250: def sgd(\\n251:     params: list[Tensor],\\n252:     d_p_list: list[Tensor],\\n253:     momentum_buffer_list: list[Optional[Tensor]],\\n254:     # kwonly args with defaults are not supported by functions compiled with torchscript issue #70627\\n255:     # setting this as kwarg for now as functional API is compiled by torch/distributed/optim\\n256:     has_sparse_grad: bool = False,\\n257:     foreach: Optional[bool] = None,\\n258:     fused: Optional[bool] = None,\\n259:     grad_scale: Optional[Tensor] = None,\\n260:     found_inf: Optional[Tensor] = None,\\n261:     *,\\n262:     weight_decay: float,\\n263:     momentum: float,\\n264:     lr: float,\\n265:     dampening: float,\\n266:     nesterov: bool,\\n267:     maximize: bool,\\n268: ):\\n269:     r\\\"\\\"\\\"Functional API that performs SGD algorithm computation.\\n270: \\n271:     See :class:`~torch.optim.SGD` for details.\\n272:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n273:     # Respect when the user inputs False/True for foreach or fused. \n186:     Nesterov momentum is based on the formula from\n187:     `On the importance of initialization and momentum in deep learning`__.\n188:     \"\"\"\n189:     + rf\"\"\"\n190:     Args:\n191: This is in contrast to some other\n242:         frameworks that initialize it to all zeros. One notable side effect\n243:         of this decision is that the first momentum value will not be scaled\n244:         by dampening. Dampening will be applied starting at the second step.\n245: \n246:     \"\"\"\n247: )\n248: \n249: \n250: def sgd(\n251:     params: list[Tensor],\n252:     d_p_list: list[Tensor],\n253:     momentum_buffer_list: list[Optional[Tensor]],\n254:     # kwonly args with defaults are not supported by functions compiled with torchscript issue #70627\n255:     # setting this as kwarg for now as functional API is compiled by torch/distributed/optim\n256:     has_sparse_grad: bool = False,\n257:     foreach: Optional[bool] = None,\n258:     fused: Optional[bool] = None,\n259:     grad_scale: Optional[Tensor] = None,\n260:     found_inf: Optional[Tensor] = None,\n261:     *,\n262:     weight_decay: float,\n263:     momentum: float,\n264:     lr: float,\n265:     dampening: float,\n266:     nesterov: bool,\n267:     maximize: bool,\n268: ):\n269:     r\"\"\"Functional API that performs SGD algorithm computation.\n270: \n271:     See :class:`~torch.optim.SGD` for details.\n272:     \"\"\"\n273:     # Respect when the user inputs False/True for foreach or fused. Iterable[tuple[str, torch.Tensor]]\\n332: ]\\n333: \\n334: R = TypeVar(\\\"R\\\")\\n335: T = TypeVar(\\\"T\\\")\\n336: \\n337: \\n338: class Optimizer:\\n339:     r\\\"\\\"\\\"Base class for all Currently needed by Adam and AdamW\\n443:     def _cuda_graph_capture_health_check(self) -> None:\\n444:         # Note [torch.compile x capturable]\\n445:         # If we are compiling, we try to take the capturable path automatically by\\n446:         # setting the flag to True during tracing. Due to this, we skip all the checks\\n447:         # normally required for determining whether we can use CUDA graphs and\\n448:         # shunt the responsibility to torch.inductor. This saves time during tracing\\n449:         # since the checks are slow without sacrificing UX since inductor will warn\\n450:         # later if CUDA graphs cannot be enabled, e.g.,\\n451:         # https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/blob/d3ba8901d8640eb16f88b2bfef9df7fa383d4b47/torch/_inductor/compile_fx.py#L390.\\n452:         # Thus, when compiling, inductor will determine if cudagraphs\\n453:         # can be enabled based on whether there is input mutation or CPU tensors.\\n454:         if (\\n455:             not torch.compiler.is_compiling()\\n456:             and torch.backends.cuda.is_built()\\n457:             and torch.cuda.is_available()\\n458:         ):\\n459:             capturing = torch.cuda.is_current_stream_capturing()\\n460: \\n461:             if capturing and not all(\\n462:                 group[\\\"capturable\\\"] for group in self.param_groups\\n463:             ):\\n464:                 raise RuntimeError(\\n465:                     \\\"Attempting CUDA graph capture of step() for an instance of \\\"\\n466:                     + self.__class__.__name__\\n467:                     + \\\" but param_groups' capturable is False.\\\"\\n468:                 )\\n469: \\n470:             if (\\n471:                 (not getattr(self, \\\"_warned_capturable_if_run_uncaptured\\\", False))\\n472:                 and all(group[\\\"capturable\\\"] for group in self.param_groups)\\n473:                 and (not capturing)\\n474:             ):\\n475:                 warnings.warn(\\n476:                     \\\"This instance was constructed with capturable=True or some of all the param_groups came with capturable=True, \\\"\\n477:                     \\\"but step() is running without CUDA graph capture. If you never intend to graph-capture this \\\"\\n478:                     \\\"instance, capturable=True can impair performance, and you should set capturable=False.\\\"\\n479:                 )\\n480:                 self._warned_capturable_if_run_uncaptured = True\\n481: \\n482:     def _optimizer_step_code(self) -> None:\\n483:         \\\"\\\"\\\"Entry point for `torch.profile.profiler`.\\n484: \\n485:         When python tracing is enabled the profiler will hook into this\\n486:         function at the CPython level to inspect the optimizer's parameters and\\n487:         param groups. It is called it after `step()` since many optimizers\\n488:         lazily initialize state.\\n489: \\n490:         This is a workaround due to lack of a proper step hook on the optimizer,\\n491:         and will be removed if it exists.\\n492:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n493: \\n494:     @staticmethod\\n495:     def profile_hook_step(func: Callable[_P, R]) -> Callable[_P, R]:  # Its content\\n673:             differs between optimizer classes, but some common characteristics\\n674:             hold. For example, state is saved per parameter, and the parameter\\n675:             itself is NOT saved. ``state`` is a Dictionary mapping parameter ids\\n676:             to a Dict with state corresponding to each parameter.\\n677:         * ``param_groups``: a List containing all parameter groups where each\\n678:             parameter group is a Dict. Each parameter group contains metadata\\n679:             specific to the optimizer, such as learning rate and weight decay,\\n680:             as well as a List of parameter IDs of the parameters in the group.\\n681:             If a param group was initialized with ``named_parameters()`` the names\\n682:             content will also be saved in the state dict.\\n683: \\n684:         NOTE: The parameter IDs may look like indices but they are just IDs\\n685:         associating state with param_group. When loading from a state_dict,\\n686:         the optimizer will zip the param_group ``params`` (int IDs) and the\\n687:         optimizer ``param_groups`` (actual ``nn.Parameter`` s) in order to\\n688:         match state WITHOUT additional verification.\\n689: \\n690:         A returned state dict might look something like:\\n691: \\n692:         .. code-block:: text\\n693: \\n694:             {\\n695:                 'state': {\\n696:                     0: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\\n697:                     1: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\\n698:                     2: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...},\\n699:                     3: {'momentum_buffer': tensor(...), ...}\\n700:                 },\\n701:                 'param_groups': [\\n702:                     {\\n703:                         'lr': 0.01,\\n704:                         'weight_decay': 0,\\n705:                         ...\\n706:                         'params': [0]\\n707:                         'param_names' ['param0']  (optional)\\n708:                     },\\n709:                     {\\n710:                         'lr': 0.001,\\n711:                         'weight_decay': 0.5,\\n712:                         ...\\n713:                         'params': [1, 2, 3]\\n714:                         'param_names': ['param1', 'layer.weight', 'layer.bias'] (optional)\\n715:                     }\\n716:                 ]\\n717:             }\\n718: \\n719:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n720:         for pre_hook in self._optimizer_state_dict_pre_hooks.values():\\n721:             pre_hook(self)\\n722: \\n723:         # Save order indices instead of Tensors\\n724:         param_mappings: dict[int, int] = {}\\n725:         start_index = 0\\n726: \\n727:         def pack_group(group: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any]:\\n728:             nonlocal start_index\\n729:             packed = {k: v for k, v in group.items() if k != \\\"params\\\"}\\n730:             param_mappings.update(\\n731:                 {\\n732:                     id(p): i\\n733:                     for i, p in enumerate(group[\\\"params\\\"], start_index)\\n734:                     if id(p) not in param_mappings\\n735:                 }\\n736:             )\\n737:             packed[\\\"params\\\"] = [param_mappings[id(p)] for p in group[\\\"params\\\"]]\\n738:             start_index += len(packed[\\\"params\\\"])\\n739:             return packed\\n740: \\n741:         param_groups = [pack_group(g) for g in self.param_groups]\\n742:         # Remap state to use order indices as keys\\n743:         packed_state = {\\n744:             (param_mappings[id(k)] if isinstance(k, torch.Tensor) else k): v\\n745:             for k, v in self.state.items()\\n746:         }\\n747: \\n748:         state_dict = {\\n749:             \\\"state\\\": packed_state,\\n750:             \\\"param_groups\\\": param_groups,\\n751:         }\\n752: \\n753:         for post_hook in self._optimizer_state_dict_post_hooks.values():\\n754:             hook_result = post_hook(self, state_dict)\\n755:             if hook_result is not None:\\n756:                 state_dict = hook_result\\n757:         return state_dict\\n758: \\n759:     @staticmethod\\n760:     def _process_value_according_to_param_policy(\\n761:         param: torch.Tensor,\\n762:         value: torch.Tensor,\\n763:         param_id: int,\\n764:         param_groups: list[dict[Any, Any]],\\n765:         key: Hashable = None,\\n766:     ) -> torch.Tensor:\\n767:         # Floating-point types are a bit special here. They are the only ones\\n768:         # that are assumed to always match the type of params.\\n769:         # Make sure state['step'] is not casted https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/74424\\n770:         # UNLESS fused or capturable, see note [special device hosting for step]\\n771:         fused = False\\n772:         capturable = False\\n773:         assert param_groups is not None\\n774:         for pg in param_groups:\\n775:             if param_id in pg[\\\"params\\\"]:\\n776:                 fused = pg[\\\"fused\\\"] if \\\"fused\\\" in pg else False\\n777:                 capturable = pg[\\\"capturable\\\"] if \\\"capturable\\\" in pg else False\\n778:                 break\\n779:         if key == \\\"step\\\":\\n780:             if capturable or fused:\\n781:                 return value.to(dtype=torch.float32, device=param.device)\\n782:             else:\\n783:                 return value\\n784:         else:\\n785:             if param.is_floating_point():\\n786:                 return value.to(dtype=param.dtype, device=param.device)\\n787:             else:\\n788:                 return value.to(device=param.device)\\n789: \\n790:     def register_load_state_dict_pre_hook(\\n791:         self,\\n792:         hook: Callable[[\\\"Optimizer\\\", StateDict], Optional[StateDict]],\\n793:         prepend: bool = False,\\n794:     ) -> RemovableHandle:  # noqa: D205 D400\\n795:         r\\\"\\\"\\\"Register a load_state_dict pre-hook which will be called before\\n796:         :meth:`~torch.optim.Optimizer.load_state_dict` is called. Its content\n673:             differs between optimizer classes, but some common characteristics\n674:             hold. For example, state is saved per parameter, and the parameter\n675:             itself is NOT saved. ``state`` is a Dictionary mapping parameter ids\n676:             to a Dict with state corresponding to each parameter.\n677:         * ``param_groups``: a List containing all parameter groups where each\n678:             parameter group is a Dict. Each parameter group contains metadata\n679:             specific to the optimizer, such as learning rate and weight decay,\n680:             as well as a List of parameter IDs of the parameters in the group.\n681:             If a param group was initialized with ``named_parameters()`` the names\n682:             content will also be saved in the state dict.\n683: \n684:         NOTE: The parameter IDs may look like indices but they are just IDs\n685:         associating state with param_group. Save order indices instead of Tensors\n724:         param_mappings: dict[int, int] = {}\n725:         start_index = 0\n726: \n727:         def pack_group(group: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any]:\n728:             nonlocal start_index\n729:             packed = {k: v for k, v in group.items() if k != \"params\"}\n730:             param_mappings.update(\n731:                 {\n732:                     id(p): i\n733:                     for i, p in enumerate(group[\"params\"], start_index)\n734:                     if id(p) not in param_mappings\n735:                 }\n736:             )\n737:             packed[\"params\"] = [param_mappings[id(p)] for p in group[\"params\"]]\n738:             start_index += len(packed[\"params\"])\n739:             return packed\n740: \n741:         param_groups = [pack_group(g) for g in self.param_groups]\n742:         # Floating-point types are a bit special here. They are the only ones\n768:         # that are assumed to always match the type of params.\n769:         # Make sure state['step'] is not casted https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/74424\n770:         # UNLESS fused or capturable, see note [special device hosting for step]\n771:         fused = False\n772:         capturable = False\n773:         assert param_groups is not None\n774:         for pg in param_groups:\n775:             if param_id in pg[\"params\"]:\n776:                 fused = pg[\"fused\"] if \"fused\" in pg else False\n777:                 capturable = pg[\"capturable\"] if \"capturable\" in pg else False\n778:                 break\n779:         if key == \"step\":\n780:             if capturable or fused:\n781:                 return value.to(dtype=torch.float32, device=param.device)\n782:             else:\n783:                 return value\n784:         else:\n785:             if param.is_floating_point():\n786:                 return value.to(dtype=param.dtype, device=param.device)\n787:             else:\n788:                 return value.to(device=param.device)\n789: \n790:     def register_load_state_dict_pre_hook(\n791:         self,\n792:         hook: Callable[[\"Optimizer\", StateDict], Optional[StateDict]],\n793:         prepend: bool = False,\n794:     ) -> RemovableHandle:  # noqa: D205 D400\n795:         r\"\"\"Register a load_state_dict pre-hook which will be called before\n796:         :meth:`~torch.optim.Optimizer.load_state_dict` is called. First step\n        noisy_optimizer.step()\n\n        # Verify step count incremented\n        self.assertEqual(noisy_optimizer.step_count, 1)\n\n        # Verify variance calculation with custom parameters\n        expected_variance_at_step_1 = eta / (1 + 1) ** gamma\n        self.assertGreater(expected_variance_at_step_1, 0)\n\n    def test_closure_support(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that step() works with a closure.\"\"\"\n        model = nn.Linear(5, 1)\n        optimizer = SGD(model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        noisy_optimizer = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n        x = torch.randn(10, 5)\n        target = torch.randn(10, 1)\n\n        def closure():\n            optimizer.zero_grad()\n            output = model(x)\n            loss = nn.MSELoss()(output, target)\n            loss.backward()\n            return loss\n\n        loss = closure()\n        loss_value = noisy_optimizer.step(closure)\n\n        # Perform a few steps to build up state\n        for _ in range(3):\n            output = model(x)\n            loss = nn.MSELoss()(output, target)\n            loss.backward()\n            noisy_optimizer.step()\n            noisy_optimizer.zero_grad()\n\n        # Learning for Very Deep Networks\"\n    technique, which adds calibrated noise to the gradients before the optimizer step.\n\n    The noise variance decays according to: sigma^2 = eta / (1 + t)^gamma\n    where t is the step count, eta is the initial noise variance, and gamma controls decay rate.\n\n    Args:\n        optimizer (Optimizer): The base optimizer to wrap\n        eta (float, optional): schedule,\n        then delegates to the base optimizer's step.\n\n        Args:\n            closure (callable, optional): A closure that reevaluates the model\n                and returns the Learning for Very Deep Networks\"\n    technique, which adds calibrated noise to the gradients before the optimizer step.\n\n    The noise variance decays according to: sigma^2 = eta / (1 + t)^gamma\n self.optimizer.param_groups:\n            for param in group[\"params\"]:\n                if param.grad is not None:\n                    # Calculate noise variance: sigma^2 = eta / (1 + t)^gamma\n torch.randn_like(param.grad) * sigma\n\n                    # Add noise to gradient\n                    param.grad.add_(noise)\n\n        # Increment step count\n        self.step_count += 1\n\n Learning for Very Deep Networks\"\n    technique, which adds calibrated noise to the gradients before the optimizer step.\n\n    The noise variance decays according to: sigma^2 = eta / (1 + t)^gamma\n `optimizer`: Base optimizer instance to wrap\n  - `eta`: Initial noise variance (default: 0.01)\n  - `gamma`: Noise decay exponent (default: 0.55)\n- `step(self, closure=None)` method that:\n  - Calculates noise variance using schedule: `sigma^2 = eta / (1 + t)^gamma`\n  - Calculate noise standard deviation: `sigma = sqrt(eta / (1 + t)^gamma)`\n2. For each parameter with gradients:\n   - Generate Gaussian noise: `noise ~ N(0, 1)` with shape matching `param.grad`\n   - Scale noise by sigma: `noise = noise * sigma`\n   - Add to gradient: `param.grad += noise`\n3. Increment step count: `t += 1`\n4. Call base optimizer's step method\n\n### Design Patterns Used\n- **Wrapper Pattern**: GradientNoiseInjector wraps a base optimizer via composition\n- **Delegation Pattern**: Unknown methods/attributes are delegated to wrapped optimizer\n- **Initialization Decay Schedule**: Noise variance decreases over time following a power law\n\n## Verification\n\nAll syntax and structure checks passed:\n- âś“ Valid Python syntax\n- âś“ Correct class structure\n- âś“ Required methods implemented\n- âś“ Proper noise schedule implementation\n- âś“ Uses torch.randn_like as specified\n- âś“ Proper registration in __init__.py\n- âś“ Comprehensive test coverage\n\n## Usage Example\n\n```python\nimport torch\nimport torch.nn as nn\nfrom torch.optim import SGD, GradientNoiseInjector\n\n# Create model\nmodel = nn.Sequential(\n    nn.Linear(10, 20),\n    nn.ReLU(),\n    nn.Linear(20, 1)\n)\n\n# Create base optimizer\noptimizer = SGD(model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n\n# Wrap with gradient noise\nnoisy_optimizer = GradientNoiseInjector(optimizer, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n# Training loop\nfor epoch in range(num_epochs):\n    for input, target in dataloader:\n        #
